	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Duke of Wellington's Regiment</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p>The <b>Duke of Wellington's Regiment (West Riding)</b> was a <a href="/wiki/Line_infantry" title="Line infantry">line</a> <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a> <a href="/wiki/Regiment" title="Regiment">regiment</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>, forming part of the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Division" title="King&#39;s Division">King's Division</a>.
</p><p>In 1702 Colonel <a href="/wiki/George_Hastings,_8th_Earl_of_Huntingdon" title="George Hastings, 8th Earl of Huntingdon">George Hastings, 8th Earl of Huntingdon</a>, was authorised to raise a new regiment, which he did in and around the city of <a href="/wiki/Gloucester" title="Gloucester">Gloucester</a>. As was the custom in those days the regiment was named <b>Huntingdon's Regiment</b> after its Colonel. As Colonel succeeded Colonel the name changed, but in 1751 regiments were given numbers, and the regiment was from that time officially known as the <b>33rd Regiment of Foot</b>. In 1782 the regiment's title was changed to the <b>33rd (or First Yorkshire West Riding) Regiment</b>, thus formalising an association with the <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="West Riding of Yorkshire">West Riding of Yorkshire</a> which, even then, had been long established. The <a href="/wiki/First_Duke_of_Wellington" class="mw-redirect" title="First Duke of Wellington">first Duke of Wellington</a> died in 1852 and in the following year <a href="/wiki/Victoria_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria of the United Kingdom">Queen Victoria</a>, in recognition of the regiment's long ties to him, ordered that the regiment's title be changed to the <b>33rd (or The Duke of Wellington's) Regiment</b>. In 1881, following the <a href="/wiki/Childers_Reforms" title="Childers Reforms">Childers Reforms</a>, the 33rd was linked with the <a href="/wiki/76th_Regiment_of_Foot" title="76th Regiment of Foot">76th Regiment of Foot</a>, who shared their depot in <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a>. The 76th had first been raised in 1745, by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Harcourt,_1st_Earl_Harcourt" title="Simon Harcourt, 1st Earl Harcourt">Simon Harcourt</a> and disbanded in 1746, re-raised in 1756 disbanded again in 1763, before being raised again in 1777, disbanded in 1784 and finally re-raised, in 1787, for service in India, by the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">Honorable East India Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The two regiments became, respectively, the 1st and 2nd battalions of the Duke of Wellington's Regiment. In 1948 the 1st and 2nd battalions were amalgamated into a single battalion, the 1st Battalion. On 6 June 2006 the 'Dukes' were amalgamated with the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales%27s_Own_Regiment_of_Yorkshire" title="Prince of Wales&#39;s Own Regiment of Yorkshire">Prince of Wales's Own Regiment of Yorkshire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Green_Howards" title="Green Howards">Green Howards</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Regiment" title="Yorkshire Regiment">Yorkshire Regiment (14th/15th, 19th and 33rd/76th Foot)</a>. As the youngest regiment the 'Dukes' became the 3rd Battalion, with each battalion retaining their antecdent regiments names in brackets. Following further mergers, in 2012, the battalion was redesignated as the new 1st Battalion (1 Yorks) of the regiment. At the same time the antecedent regimental names were dropped from the battalion titles.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Battalions from the regiment had served in most land conflicts involving British forces since its formation, from the Wars of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">Austrian</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">Spanish</a> successions, through the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American war of Independence</a> and various campaigns in India and Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a> and many of the greatest battles of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mons" title="Battle of Mons">Battle of Mons</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Battle of the Somme</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Passchendaele" title="Battle of Passchendaele">Battle of Passchendaele</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cambrai_(1917)" title="Battle of Cambrai (1917)">Battle of Cambrai</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Afghan_War" title="Third Anglo-Afghan War">Third Anglo-Afghan War</a> in 1919. During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, the regiment fought as part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Expeditionary_Force_(World_War_II)" title="British Expeditionary Force (World War II)">British Expeditionary Force</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, forming part of the rearguard at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dunkirk" title="Battle of Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a>; in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>; <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, following the <a href="/wiki/D-Day" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Day">D-Day</a> landings, and as <a href="/wiki/Chindits" title="Chindits">Chindits</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burma</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korea</a>, the 'Dukes' desperate defence of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Hook" title="Battle of the Hook">Hook</a> position halted the last major Chinese attempt to break the United Nations Line before the truce, in July 1953, brought the war to an end. In Cyprus the battalion was successful in Operation Golden Rain, destroying a major <a href="/wiki/EOKA" title="EOKA">EOKA</a> terrorist group operating in the Troodos Mountains in 1956. In 1964 the battalion joined the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> deterrence in Germany on the front line in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> and from 1971 was regularly engaged in '<a href="/wiki/The_Troubles" title="The Troubles">The Troubles</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> until 1997. They were amongst the first units to cross the border from <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a> in the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>.
</p><p>Nine soldiers from the regiment have been awarded the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Cross" title="Victoria Cross">Victoria Cross</a>, and Corporal <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Mills_(British_Army_soldier)" title="Wayne Mills (British Army soldier)">Wayne Mills</a> of the 1st Battalion became the first recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Conspicuous_Gallantry_Cross" title="Conspicuous Gallantry Cross">Conspicuous Gallantry Cross</a> in 1994, whilst serving with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> forces in <a href="/wiki/Bosnia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnia">Bosnia</a>.
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_and_name">Formation and name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Formation and name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="floatleft"><a href="/wiki/File:DWR_33rd_Badge_(RLH).jpg" class="image" title="33rd Regiment Insignia"><img alt="33rd Regiment Insignia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/DWR_33rd_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg/90px-DWR_33rd_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="90" height="121" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/DWR_33rd_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg/135px-DWR_33rd_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/DWR_33rd_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg/180px-DWR_33rd_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="199" data-file-height="267" /></a></div>
<p><b>The Duke of Wellington's Regiment</b> was originally formed in 1702 as <b>Huntingdon's Regiment</b>. As regiments at that time took the name of the Colonel taking it over it became:- <b>Henry Leigh's Regiment</b>; then <b>Robert Duncansons Regiment</b> and <b>George Wade's Regiment</b>. It was disbanded on 25 March 1714, but was officially registered as the <b>33rd Regiment of Foot</b> in January 1715 and re-raised on 25 March 1715, as <b>George Wade's Regiment</b>; then <b>Henry Hawley's Regiment</b>; <b>Robert Dalzell's Regiment</b> and <b>John Johnson's Regiment</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-brief-history_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief-history-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1782 Lord Cornwallis, the then Colonel of the Regiment, wrote that "The 33rd Regiment of Infantry has always recruited in the West Riding of Yorkshire and has a very good interest and the general goodwill of the people in that part of the country:-   I should therefore wish not only to be permitted to recruit in that county, but that my Regiment may bear the name of the 33rd or West Yorkshire Regiment".  On 31 August 1782 Lord Cornwallis heard that the King had approved of the new title:-  <b>33rd (or the 1st West Yorkshire West Riding) Regiment of Foot</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-brief-history_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief-history-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Owing to its links with the <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Duke of Wellington</a>, the title 'The Duke of Wellington's Regiment' was granted to the 33rd Regiment on 18 June 1853, on the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a> in the year following Wellington's death.<sup id="cite_ref-brief-history_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief-history-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/76th_Regiment_of_Foot" title="76th Regiment of Foot">76th Regiment of Foot</a></div>
<div class="floatleft"><a href="/wiki/File:DWR_76th_Badge_(RLH).jpg" class="image" title="76th Regiment Insignia"><img alt="76th Regiment Insignia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/DWR_76th_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg/90px-DWR_76th_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="90" height="152" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/DWR_76th_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg/135px-DWR_76th_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/DWR_76th_Badge_%28RLH%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="158" data-file-height="267" /></a></div>
<p>The 76th Regiment was originally raised, by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Harcourt,_1st_Earl_Harcourt" title="Simon Harcourt, 1st Earl Harcourt">Simon Harcourt</a> as <b>Lord Harcourt's Regiment</b> on 17 November 1745 and disbanded in June 1746. Following the loss of <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a>, to the French, it was reraised in November 1756 as the <b>61st Regiment</b>, but renumbered to 76th, by General Order in 1758, and again disbanded in 1763. A second battalion raised by that regiment in October 1758, for service in Africa, was renumbered as the 86th Regiment  and also disbanded in 1763. On 25 December 1777, the 76th was again re-raised, as the <b>76th Regiment of Foot (Macdonald's Highlanders)</b>, by Colonel John MacDonell of Lochgarry, in the West of Scotland and Western Isles, as a Scottish Light Infantry regiment. It was disbanded at <a href="/wiki/Stirling_Castle" title="Stirling Castle">Stirling Castle</a> in March 1784. The regiment was again raised for service in India by the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">Honorable East India Company</a> in 1787.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1881 the 76th Regiment, which shared the same Depot in <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a> as the 33rd, was linked to the 33rd, under the <a href="/wiki/Childers_Reforms" title="Childers Reforms">Childers Reforms</a>, to become the 2nd Battalion. Although retitled as the <b>Halifax Regiment (Duke of Wellington's)</b> this title only lasted six months until it was changed on 30 June 1881, in a revised appendix to General order 41, to:- <b>The Duke of Wellington's (West Riding Regiment)</b>, or 'W Rid R' for short. In January 1921 it was again retitled to <b>The Duke of Wellington's Regiment (West Riding)</b>, or 'DWR' for short.<sup id="cite_ref-brief-history_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief-history-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span id="1702.E2.80.931881"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1702–1881">1702–1881</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1702–1881">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldier_of_33rd_regiment_1742.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Soldier_of_33rd_regiment_1742.jpg/220px-Soldier_of_33rd_regiment_1742.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="376" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Soldier_of_33rd_regiment_1742.jpg/330px-Soldier_of_33rd_regiment_1742.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/Soldier_of_33rd_regiment_1742.jpg 2x" data-file-width="353" data-file-height="604" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soldier_of_33rd_regiment_1742.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soldier of 33rd regiment, 1742</div></div></div>
<p>Within months of its original raising the regiment was despatched to join <a href="/wiki/John_Churchill,_1st_Duke_of_Marlborough" title="John Churchill, 1st Duke of Marlborough">Marlborough</a>'s army in Holland. After five months and only two battles it was sent to Portugal, along with five other of Malborough's best regiments, where it remained for the next six years. The 33rd fought in many battles including Valencia de Alcantara (1705), Zaragossa (1710), and less favourably at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Almansa" title="Battle of Almansa">Almansa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Brihuega" title="Battle of Brihuega">Brihuega</a>. It was only one of the two foot regiments not to be disbanded and in 1743 the regiment was sent to Germany, where it distinguished itself in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dettingen" title="Battle of Dettingen">Battle of Dettingen</a>, gaining its first <a href="/wiki/Battle_honour" title="Battle honour">battle honour</a>, then again at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fontenoy" title="Battle of Fontenoy">Battle of Fontenoy</a> in 1745 and again in Rocoux and Lauffeld in 1747.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> During the late 18th century, the regiment gained the familiar nickname <b>The Havercakes</b>, due to its <a href="/wiki/Sergeant" title="Sergeant">sergeants</a> carrying <a href="/wiki/Oatcake" title="Oatcake">oatcakes</a> on the tip of their swords to attract new recruits.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Revolution">American Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: American Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 33rd itself had a good reputation for its professionalism and capability, which was seemingly unequalled by any other regiment of the British Army for some time. It was because of their  professionalism in the field during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a>, that the regiment was given the nickname 'The Pattern'; the regiment then became the standard of soldiering which all other regiments should attain.<sup id="cite_ref-american_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-american-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 33rd saw much action during the American War of Independence, with its first engagement at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sullivan%27s_Island" title="Battle of Sullivan&#39;s Island">Battle of Sullivan's Island</a> (First Siege of Charleston) in early 1776, when British forces attempted an assault on that city's defences, resulting in a disastrous British defeat. In August of that year, the 33rd were involved in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Long_Island" title="Battle of Long Island">Battle of Long Island</a>, in which a heavy defeat was inflicted on the Americans, who evacuated their remaining forces to the island of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33foot_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33foot-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The regiment's next action came a fortnight later, on September 16th at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Harlem_Heights" title="Battle of Harlem Heights">Battle of Harlem Heights</a>. After the British had landed and seized New York, a force of British light infantry pursuing an American scouting patrol advanced too far from their lines and found itself in danger of being cut off in an unexpected counter attack.  The 33rd formed part of Lord Cornwallis' Reserve Corps sent in support to cover their withdrawal.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The regiment was also involved in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Washington" title="Battle of Fort Washington">Battle of Fort Washington</a>. After that, the 33rd were not involved in a major battle until September 1777, when they took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Brandywine" title="Battle of Brandywine">Battle of Brandywine</a>, where the British suffered 550 casualties and the Americans about 1,000. The regiment took part in further action that year, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Germantown" title="Battle of Germantown">Battle of Germantown</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_White_Marsh" title="Battle of White Marsh">Battle of White Marsh</a>, where they fought the Americans who had retreated from the fighting at Germantown.<sup id="cite_ref-33foot_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33foot-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The following year was just as active, with the 33rd seeing action at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monmouth" title="Battle of Monmouth">Battle of Monmouth</a>, an inclusive engagement that became the largest one-day battle of the war.  The 33rd was also part of the defence of <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quaker_Hill,_New_York" title="Quaker Hill, New York">Quaker Hill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33foot_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33foot-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two years later, in 1780, the 33rd took part in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Charleston" title="Siege of Charleston">Siege of Charleston</a>. By 11 May, the American General <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Lincoln" title="Benjamin Lincoln">Benjamin Lincoln</a> began to negotiate terms of surrender. The following day Lincoln, along with over 7,000 American soldiers, surrendered to the British forces under the command of Lieutenant-General <a href="/wiki/Henry_Clinton_(1730%E2%80%931795)" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Clinton (1730–1795)">Henry Clinton</a>. In August that year, the 33rd were involved at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Camden" title="Battle of Camden">Battle of Camden</a>, a victory for the British.<sup id="cite_ref-33foot_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33foot-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Guilford_Court_House">Guilford Court House</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Guilford Court House">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guilford_Court_House" title="Battle of Guilford Court House">Battle of Guilford Court House</a></div>
<p>The year 1781 proved to be the deadliest but most successful year for the 33rd. The regiment took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wetzell%27s_Mill" title="Battle of Wetzell&#39;s Mill">Battle of Wetzell's Mill</a> (inconclusive), but the more famous action took place that same month during a battle at Guilford Court House.<sup id="cite_ref-courthouse_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courthouse-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse_15_March_1781_(DWR).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse_15_March_1781_%28DWR%29.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse_15_March_1781_%28DWR%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse_15_March_1781_%28DWR%29.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse_15_March_1781_%28DWR%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse_15_March_1781_%28DWR%29.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse_15_March_1781_%28DWR%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="766" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Guilford_Courthouse_15_March_1781_(DWR).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Guilford Court House Battleground</div></div></div>
<p>On 14 March 1781, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Cornwallis,_1st_Marquess_Cornwallis" title="Charles Cornwallis, 1st Marquess Cornwallis">Lord Cornwallis</a>, the British commander, was informed that General <a href="/wiki/Richard_Butler_(general)" title="Richard Butler (general)">Richard Butler</a> was marching to attack his army. With Butler was a body of <a href="/wiki/Province_of_North_Carolina" title="Province of North Carolina">North Carolina</a> <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">Militia</a>, plus reinforcements from <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, consisting of 3,000 Virginia Militia, a Virginia State regiment, a Corp of Virginian "eighteen-month men" and recruits for the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Line" title="Maryland Line">Maryland Line</a>. They had joined the command of Major General <a href="/wiki/Nathanael_Greene" title="Nathanael Greene">Nathanael Greene</a>, creating a force of some four to 5 thousand men in total. During the night, further reports confirmed the American force was at Guilford Court House, some 12 miles (20&#160;km) away. Cornwallis decided to give battle, though he had only 1,900 men at his disposal.<sup id="cite_ref-courthouse_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courthouse-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornwallis_Re-enactment_Coy_33rd_Regt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Cornwallis_Re-enactment_Coy_33rd_Regt.jpg/220px-Cornwallis_Re-enactment_Coy_33rd_Regt.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="284" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Cornwallis_Re-enactment_Coy_33rd_Regt.jpg/330px-Cornwallis_Re-enactment_Coy_33rd_Regt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Cornwallis_Re-enactment_Coy_33rd_Regt.jpg/440px-Cornwallis_Re-enactment_Coy_33rd_Regt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="464" data-file-height="598" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cornwallis_Re-enactment_Coy_33rd_Regt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>33rd Regiment at a reenactment</div></div></div>
<p>At dawn on 15 March 1781, before the men had a chance to have breakfast, Cornwallis started for Guilford, arriving there at mid-day.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cornwallis' troops included Bose's Hessian Regiment and the 71st commanded by Major General <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Leslie_(British_Army_officer)" title="Alexander Leslie (British Army officer)">Alexander Leslie</a> and the 23rd and 33rd commanded by Lieutenant Colonel James Webster of the 33rd. The second line comprised the two battalions of Foot Guards, the Light Infantry and the Grenadiers commanded by Brigadier <a href="/wiki/Charles_O%27Hara" title="Charles O&#39;Hara">Charles O'Hara</a> of the 2nd Coldstream Regiment of Foot Guards. There was then a reserve consisting of Tarleton's Light Dragoons.<sup id="cite_ref-courthouse_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courthouse-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The British troops advanced under heavy musket fire. Webster attacked the right flank of the American second line and managed to push it back. He also attacked the American third line. An American counterattack then led to a confused situation. Meanwhile, Tarleton's Light Dragoons charged the right flank.<sup id="cite_ref-courthouse_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courthouse-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The American troops then withdrew. The British technically defeated the American force, but Webster was killed and O'Hara was wounded, along with 27% of the British force.<sup id="cite_ref-courthouse_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courthouse-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_Spring">Green Spring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Green Spring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The 33rd also fought at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Green_Spring" title="Battle of Green Spring">Battle of Green Spring</a> in July of that year, where they defeated an American force that was outnumbered by approximately 6,000 men.<sup id="cite_ref-33foot_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33foot-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Their last engagement of the war was at the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown" title="Siege of Yorktown">Siege of Yorktown</a>, when they were part of the outnumbered British forces.<sup id="cite_ref-33foot_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33foot-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flanders">Flanders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Flanders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1793 <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Arthur Wesley</a>, the third son of the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Mornington" title="Earl of Mornington">Earl of Mornington</a> and future <a href="/wiki/Dukes_of_Wellington" class="mw-redirect" title="Dukes of Wellington">Duke of Wellington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purchase_of_commissions_in_the_British_Army" title="Purchase of commissions in the British Army">purchased a commission</a> in the 33rd as a <a href="/wiki/Major_(British_Army)" class="mw-redirect" title="Major (British Army)">Major</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmes25_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes25-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> A few months later, in September, his brother lent him more money and with it he purchased a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_colonel" title="Lieutenant colonel">lieutenant-colonelcy</a> in the 33rd.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmes28_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes28-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The regiment took part in the disastrous <a href="/wiki/Flanders_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Flanders Campaign">Flanders Campaign</a> and the retreat from Germany, and embarked, from <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a>, for England on 13 April 1795.<sup id="cite_ref-brief_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Wesley was promoted to full <a href="/wiki/Colonel_(British_Army)" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonel (British Army)">Colonel</a> by seniority on 3 May 1796<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and changed his name to Arthur Wellesley in 1798.<sup id="cite_ref-Holmes41_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holmes41-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1799 the regiment took part in the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Mysore_War" title="Fourth Anglo-Mysore War">Fourth Anglo-Mysore War</a> in a Division commanded by Colonel Arthur Wellesley, as part of a <a href="/wiki/British_East_India_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="British East India Company">British East India Company</a> army, commanded by Major General Harris, with Major General Sir David Baird as second in command. Arthur's eldest brother Richard Wellesley, 2nd Earl of Mornington, later 1st Marquess Wellesley, had just become Governor General of India. So in addition to the 33rd, Arthur, who had now become Colonel Arthur Wellesley, was given command of the 10,000 men of the <a href="/wiki/Nizam_of_Hyderabad" title="Nizam of Hyderabad">Nizam of Hyderabad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> They had a decisive part to play in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Seringapatam" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Seringapatam">Battle of Seringapatam</a>. The regiment, involved in bitter fighting with the <a href="/wiki/Tippu_Sultan" class="mw-redirect" title="Tippu Sultan">Tippu Sultan</a>'s warriors, were repulsed with heavy losses when they attacked a wood, which was strongly defended by the Sultan's forces. The 33rd rallied and fought further actions throughout the battle, with the British emerging decisively victorious and the Tippoo Sultan being killed. The regiment won a battle honour for its involvement in the action.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Napoleon.27s_Return_and_Waterloo"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Napoleon's_Return_and_Waterloo">Napoleon's Return and Waterloo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Napoleon&#039;s Return and Waterloo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wellingtons33rd.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Wellingtons33rd.jpg/220px-Wellingtons33rd.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Wellingtons33rd.jpg/330px-Wellingtons33rd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Wellingtons33rd.jpg/440px-Wellingtons33rd.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="869" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wellingtons33rd.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reenactors in the red-coated uniform of the <a href="/wiki/33rd_Regiment_of_Foot" class="mw-redirect" title="33rd Regiment of Foot">33rd Regiment of Foot</a> as worn during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> between 1812 and 1816. Note the brighter scarlet of the officer on the right.</div></div></div>
<p>By early March 1815, the regiment was again under the command of the Duke of Wellington, this time during the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days" title="Hundred Days">Hundred Days</a> campaign of Napoleon.  Having taken part in the action of the previous day, at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Quatre_Bras" title="Battle of Quatre Bras">Battle of Quatre Bras</a>, they took part in the action at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Waterloo</a>; the 33rd was part of the 5th Brigade under the command of <a href="/wiki/Major_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Major General">Major General</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/Colin_Halkett" title="Colin Halkett">Colin Halkett</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="West_Indies">West Indies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: West Indies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Having departed from Paris on 23 December 1815, the regiment spent the post Waterloo period, from January 1816 to 1821, in uneventful garrison duties in <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stirling" title="Stirling">Stirling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-peace_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peace-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1822, the regiment was posted to <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">West Indies</a> were notorious as the death bed of the British Army because of the high mortality rate from <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a> and other such endemic diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-peace_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peace-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crimea">Crimea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Crimea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Owing to its links with Wellington, the title <b>33rd (The Duke of Wellington's) Regiment</b> was granted to the 33rd, on 18 June 1853 (the 38th Anniversary of the Battle of Waterloo) by <a href="/wiki/Victoria_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria of the United Kingdom">Queen Victoria</a>, in honour of the 1st Duke of Wellington, who had died on 14 September the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alma" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Alma">Battle of Alma</a>, bitter fighting took place, with the 33rd being part of the Light Division under the command of <a href="/wiki/George_Brown_(British_Army_officer)" title="George Brown (British Army officer)">Sir George Brown</a>. The British advanced up the slope towards the Russian positions. The British formations became intermingled, turning into a mass of soldiers, rather than the professional, neat formations used on parade. As they charged, numerous Russian troops came down the slope to meet them. The British halted and fired, causing so many casualties the Russians were forced to retreat. The British line reorganised and moved up the slope towards the Great Redoubt, with the 33rd being the first to attack the defence works. The 33rd suffered heavy casualties: 7 officers and 232 men in the hand-to-hand combat that ensued.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Inkerman" title="Battle of Inkerman">Battle of Inkerman</a>, the 33rd were again involved in some bitter fighting, in which the British infantry advanced despite heavy losses and a strong defence by the Russians. The fighting was fierce, at times some soldiers resorting to attacking their enemy with the butts of their guns.  The 33rd suffered further casualties: 3 officers and 61 men.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 33rd was involved in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1854%E2%80%931855)" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1854–1855)">Siege of Sevastopol</a>, which lasted for 11 months. By 1856, the war was over but for little gain.<sup id="cite_ref-crimea_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimea-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abyssinia">Abyssinia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Abyssinia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1868_Expedition_to_Abyssinia" class="mw-redirect" title="1868 Expedition to Abyssinia">1868 Expedition to Abyssinia</a></div>
<p>The 33rd were part of an expedition sent to the East African nation of Abyssinia, now known as <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> after several European citizens had been taken hostage by the self-appointed 'King' <a href="/wiki/Tewodros_II" title="Tewodros II">Emperor Tewodros II</a> in 1864. In March 1866 a British <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">envoy</a> had been despatched to secure the release of a group of <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> who had first been seized after the British Government refused Tewdros’s requests for military assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-crimea_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crimea-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 33rd was committed to Abyssinia in October 1867 and embarked on 21 November, arriving at Annesley Bay on 4 December; but did not disembark for three days due to the chaos on shore.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Magdala_Landscape_Composite_(RLH).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Magdala_Landscape_Composite_%28RLH%29.jpg/220px-Magdala_Landscape_Composite_%28RLH%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="55" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Magdala_Landscape_Composite_%28RLH%29.jpg/330px-Magdala_Landscape_Composite_%28RLH%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Magdala_Landscape_Composite_%28RLH%29.jpg/440px-Magdala_Landscape_Composite_%28RLH%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9960" data-file-height="2478" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Magdala_Landscape_Composite_(RLH).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The plateau at Arogye, across the route to Magdala</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Napier,_1st_Baron_Napier_of_Magdala" title="Robert Napier, 1st Baron Napier of Magdala">Lord Napier</a> arrived in early January 1868 and the expedition started from the advance camp at <a href="/wiki/Senafe" title="Senafe">Senafe</a> at the beginning of February. It took two months to reach their objective, advancing through rough terrain. In his despatch to London Lord Napier reported: "Yesterday morning (we) descended three thousand nine hundred feet to <a href="/wiki/Bashilo_River" title="Bashilo River">Bashilo River</a> and approached <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Magdala" title="Battle of Magdala">Magdala</a> with 'First Brigade' to reconnoiter it.  Theodore opened fire with seven guns from outwork, one thousand feet above us, and three thousand five hundred men of the garrison made a gallant sortie which was repulsed with very heavy loss and the enemy driven into Magdala. British loss, twenty wounded".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As the British force moved on to Magdala, Tewodros II sent two of the hostages on parole to offer terms.  Napier insisted on the release of all the hostages and an unconditional surrender. Tewodros refused to cede to the unconditional surrender, but did release the European hostages.  The British continued the advance and assaulted the fortress. (The native hostages were later found to have had their hands and feet cut off before being sent over the edge of the precipice surrounding the plateau.)<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On reaching the gate there was a pause in the advance, as it was discovered the engineer unit had forgot their powder kegs and scaling ladders and were ordered to return for them. General <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Dunbar_Staveley" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles William Dunbar Staveley">Staveley</a> was not happy at any further delay and ordered the 33rd to continue the attack. Several officers and the men of the 33rd Regiment, along with an officer from the Royal Engineers, parted from the main force and, after climbing the cliff face, found their way blocked by a thorny hedge over a wall. Private <a href="/wiki/James_Bergin" title="James Bergin">James Bergin</a>, a very tall man, used his bayonet to cut a hole in the hedge and Drummer <a href="/wiki/Michael_Magner" title="Michael Magner">Michael Magner</a> climbed onto his shoulders through the hedge in the gap and dragged Bergin up behind him as Ensign Conner and Corporal Murphy helped shove from below.  Bergin kept up a rapid rate of fire on the Koket-Bir as Magner dragged more men through the gap in the hedge. As more men poured through and opened fire as they advanced with their bayonets the defenders withdrew through the second gate. The party rushed the Koket-bir before it was fully closed and then took the second gate breaking through to the Amba. Ensign Wynter scrambled up onto the top of the second gate and fixed the 33rd Regiments Colours to show the Plateau had been taken.  Private Bergin and Drummer Magner were later awarded the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Cross" title="Victoria Cross">Victoria Cross</a> for their part in the action.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tewodros II was found dead inside the second gate, having shot himself with a pistol that had been a gift from Queen Victoria. When his death was announced all opposition ceased. The regiment later received the battle honour <a href="/wiki/Abyssinia_(battle_honour)" title="Abyssinia (battle honour)">Abyssinia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Volunteers">Volunteers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Volunteers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The invasion scare of 1859 led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_Force_(Great_Britain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Volunteer Force (Great Britain)">Volunteer Force</a> and huge enthusiasm for joining local Rifle Volunteer Corps (RVCs).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> A large number of individual RVCs were raised in the West Riding; some amalgamated into larger units, and the rest of the smaller units were grouped into administrative battalions. For example, the RVCs raised in <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a> were amalgamated as the 4th Yorkshire (West Riding) RVC in 1860. The senior unit in the 5th Admin Bn at <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a> was the 6th Yorkshire (West Riding) RVC, officially entitled the <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rifles" title="Huddersfield Rifles">Huddersfield Rifles</a> in 1868. In 1880 the 5th Admin Bn was consolidated as a new <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rifles" title="Huddersfield Rifles">6th Yorkshire (West Riding) RVC</a>. Similarly, the 2nd Admin Bn at <a href="/wiki/Skipton-in-Craven" class="mw-redirect" title="Skipton-in-Craven">Skipton-in-Craven</a> was consolidated as a new 9th Yorkshire (West Riding) RVC in 1880.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Westlake_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Westlake-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Childers_Reforms.2C_1881-"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Childers_Reforms,_1881-">Childers Reforms, 1881-</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Childers Reforms, 1881-">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Childers_Reforms" title="Childers Reforms">Childers Reforms</a> (and as a continuation of the <a href="/wiki/Cardwell_Reforms" title="Cardwell Reforms">Cardwell Reforms</a>) brought the <a href="/wiki/Militia_(United_Kingdom)" title="Militia (United Kingdom)">Militia</a> into the regimental system, and the two battalions of 6th West York Militia became the 3rd and 4th Battalions of the Duke of Wellington's.<sup id="cite_ref-regimentsDoW_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regimentsDoW-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>  The Duke of Wellington’s Regiment (33rd) was amalgamated with the 76th to become the 1st and 2nd Battalions.<sup id="cite_ref-TheDukes_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheDukes-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the same time the three West Riding Volunteer battalions became linked with the Regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-TheDukes_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheDukes-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In February 1883, as part of the Childers Reforms, these three corps were designated as the 1st, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rifles" title="Huddersfield Rifles">2nd</a> and 3rd Volunteer Battalions of the Duke of Wellington's Regiment. By 1887 they had adopted the same uniform as the parent unit.<sup id="cite_ref-Westlake_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Westlake-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Under the mobilisation scheme introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Stanhope_Memorandum" title="Stanhope Memorandum">Stanhope Memorandum</a> of December 1888 the Volunteer Battalions of the Duke of Wellington's were assigned to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Yorkshire_Volunteer_Infantry_Brigade&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="West Yorkshire Volunteer Infantry Brigade (page does not exist)">West Yorkshire Volunteer Infantry Brigade</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Command_(United_Kingdom)" title="Northern Command (United Kingdom)">Northern Command</a> and in the event of war were expected to mobilise at <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Duties_of_Empire_.281881.E2.80.931914.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Duties_of_Empire_(1881–1914)">Duties of Empire (1881–1914)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Duties of Empire (1881–1914)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment_by_Harry_Payne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment_by_Harry_Payne.jpg/220px-The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment_by_Harry_Payne.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="343" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment_by_Harry_Payne.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="468" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment_by_Harry_Payne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Uniforms of The Duke of Wellington's Regiment as worn 1902–14, by <a href="/wiki/Harry_Payne_(artist)" title="Harry Payne (artist)">Harry Payne</a></div></div></div>
<p>The 2nd battalion was stationed at <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> from 1886, transferred to <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax, Nova Scotia</a> in 1888, then to the West Indies in 1891. In April 1893 the battalion, under Lt-Col. E. Nesbitt, set sail for the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>, posting one company on <a href="/wiki/St_Helena" class="mw-redirect" title="St Helena">St Helena</a> en route. In October a detachment of 3 officers and 51 NCOs and men were despatched up-country to serve with the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Police_Service" title="Botswana Police Service">Bechuanaland Border Police</a> in the <a href="/wiki/First_Matabele_War" title="First Matabele War">Matabele Uprising</a>, in a complicated arrangement due to the fact that the BPP was at the time run by the <a href="/wiki/British_South_Africa_Company" title="British South Africa Company">British South Africa Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bruce_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bruce-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some detachments of the battalion stayed on to serve in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Matabele_War" title="Second Matabele War">Second Matabele War</a> (1896-7), being stationed in the colony of <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Natal" title="Colony of Natal">Natal</a> in between. 13 Officers and 320 NCOs and men proceeded on active service. Some served on the staff, some with mounted infantry, some with the Matabeleland Relief Force and other service companies.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bruce_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bruce-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The battalion was sent to India in 1897.
</p><p>The regiment began the first year of the 20th century at war when both battalions met in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, as reinforcements for British forces fighting <a href="/wiki/Boer" title="Boer">Boers</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a>. The 1st battalion had arrived there before war started in 1899, the 2nd battalion arrived in early 1900, and took part in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Kimberley" title="Siege of Kimberley">Relief of Kimberley</a>, in February 1900, which had been under siege by the Boers since October 1899. The battalion also took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Paardeberg" title="Battle of Paardeberg">Battle of Paardeberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The 3rd (Militia) Battalion (the former 6th West York Militia) was embodied in January 1900 for service in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, and 500 officers and men left <a href="/wiki/Cobh" title="Cobh">Queenstown</a> for <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a> the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Most of the battalion returned to the United Kingdom in late May 1902.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All three Volunteer Battalions also sent service companies to support the Regular battalions, and received the Battle Honour <b>South Africa 1900–1902</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the end of the war in South Africa, the 1st battalion returned to York, while the 2nd battalion went to <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a>, first to <a href="/wiki/Rangoon" class="mw-redirect" title="Rangoon">Rangoon</a> then in late 1902 to <a href="/wiki/Lebong" title="Lebong">Lebong</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bengal_Presidency" title="Bengal Presidency">Bengal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_Force">Territorial Force</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Territorial Force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Force" title="Territorial Force">Territorial Force</a> (TF) was formed under the <a href="/wiki/Haldane_Reforms" title="Haldane Reforms">Haldane Reforms</a> in 1908, Volunteer Battalions were renumbered as battalions of their parent regiments. The Duke of Wellington's 1st VB became the 4th Battalion at <a href="/wiki/Prescott_Street_drill_hall,_Halifax" title="Prescott Street drill hall, Halifax">Prescott Street</a> in Halifax. The 2nd VB formed two new battalions: the <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rifles" title="Huddersfield Rifles">5th Battalion</a> at <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Street_drill_hall,_Huddersfield" title="St Paul&#39;s Street drill hall, Huddersfield">St Paul's Street</a> in Huddersfield, and the 7th Battalion at <a href="/wiki/Scar_Lane_drill_hall,_Milnsbridge" title="Scar Lane drill hall, Milnsbridge">Scar Lane</a> in <a href="/wiki/Milnsbridge" title="Milnsbridge">Milnsbridge</a>. The 3rd VB became the 6th Battalion at <a href="/wiki/Otley_Road_drill_hall,_Skipton" title="Otley Road drill hall, Skipton">Otley Road</a> in Skipton. The former West Yorkshire Brigade was split in two, and the four TF battalions of the Duke of Wellington's Regiment composed the new <a href="/wiki/147th_(2nd_West_Riding)_Brigade" class="mw-redirect" title="147th (2nd West Riding) Brigade">2nd West Riding Brigade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/49th_(West_Riding)_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="49th (West Riding) Division">West Riding Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Westlake_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Westlake-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Regts7_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts7-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Becke49_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Becke49-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="First_World_War">First World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: First World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regular_Army">Regular Army</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Regular Army">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1st Battalion remained in India throughout the war, serving first with the <a href="/wiki/2nd_(Rawalpindi)_Division" title="2nd (Rawalpindi) Division">2nd (Rawalpindi) Division</a> and then with the <a href="/wiki/1st_(Peshawar)_Division" title="1st (Peshawar) Division">1st (Peshawar) Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-trail_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trail-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2nd Battalion landed at <a href="/wiki/Le_Havre" title="Le Havre">Le Havre</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/13th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="13th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">13th Brigade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/5th_Infantry_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="5th Infantry Division (United Kingdom)">5th Division</a> in August 1914 for service on the  <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-trail_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trail-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> It first saw action at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mons" title="Battle of Mons">Battle of Mons</a>. It then fought a rearguard action at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Le_Cateau" title="Battle of Le Cateau">Battle of Le Cateau</a>, an action during the <a href="/wiki/Retreat_from_Mons" class="mw-redirect" title="Retreat from Mons">retreat from Mons</a>. The 2nd Battalion also fought at the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_the_Marne" title="First Battle of the Marne">First Battle of the Marne</a>, the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_the_Aisne" title="First Battle of the Aisne">Battle of the Aisne</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_La_Bass%C3%A9e" title="Battle of La Bassée">Battle of La Bassée</a> and the brutal first <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Ypres" title="First Battle of Ypres">Battle of Ypres</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ww1_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww1-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The 2nd Battalion was also at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hill_60_(Western_Front)" title="Battle of Hill 60 (Western Front)">Battle of Hill 60</a> during which the British launched a massive bombardment, followed by an assault that led to vicious hand-to-hand fighting. The 8th Battalion saw service in the <a href="/wiki/Gallipoli_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallipoli Campaign">Gallipoli Campaign</a> and the 10th Battalion was in action at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Piave_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of the Piave River">Piave</a> in Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-ww1_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww1-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_Force_2">Territorial Force</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Territorial Force">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1/4th, 1/5th, 1/6th and 1/7 th battalions landed in France as part of the <a href="/wiki/147th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="147th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">147th (2nd West Riding) Brigade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/49th_(West_Riding)_Infantry_Division" title="49th (West Riding) Infantry Division">49th (West Riding) Division</a> in April 1915 for service on the Western Front and served together until the <a href="/wiki/Armistice_of_11_November_1918" title="Armistice of 11 November 1918">Armistice</a> in November 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-trail_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trail-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> They saw action on the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Somme</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Passchendaele" title="Battle of Passchendaele">Ypres</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Spring_Offensive" title="Spring Offensive">German Spring Offensive</a> and the final Allied <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days_Offensive" title="Hundred Days Offensive">Hundred Days Offensive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Becke49_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Becke49-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 1914 the Territorial Force formed 2nd Line units, distinguished from the 1st Line by the addition of '2/' to the battalion number, the parent units taking '1/'. The 2/4th, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rifles" title="Huddersfield Rifles">2/5th</a>, 2/6th and 2/7th Battalions of the Duke of Wellingtons formed <a href="/wiki/186th_(2/2nd_West_Riding)_Brigade" title="186th (2/2nd West Riding) Brigade">186th (2/2nd West Riding) Brigade</a> in <a href="/wiki/62nd_(2nd_West_Riding)_Division" title="62nd (2nd West Riding) Division">62nd (2nd West Riding) Division</a>. The division's training was hampered by the lack of equipment and by the need to provide drafts to the 1st Line units serving overseas, but finally landed in France in January 1917 and served on the Western Front until the Armistice.<sup id="cite_ref-trail_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trail-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> It fought at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arras_(1917)" title="Battle of Arras (1917)">Arras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cambrai_(1917)" title="Battle of Cambrai (1917)">Cambrai</a>, in the Spring Offensive and the Hundred Days, and was the only TF division selected to form part of the Allied occupation force in the Rhineland after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Territorial Force battalions also formed 3rd Line units, which remained in the UK training and supplying drafts for the battalions overseas.<sup id="cite_ref-trail_54-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trail-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Armies">New Armies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: New Armies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 8th (Service) Battalion landed at <a href="/wiki/Suvla" title="Suvla">Suvla Bay</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gallipoli" title="Gallipoli">Gallipoli</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/32nd_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="32nd Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">32nd Brigade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/11th_(Northern)_Division" title="11th (Northern) Division">11th (Northern) Division</a> in August 1915; the battalion  was evacuated in January 1916 and moved to France in July 1916 for service on the Western Front.<sup id="cite_ref-trail_54-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trail-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The 9th (Service) Battalion landed at <a href="/wiki/Boulogne-sur-Mer" title="Boulogne-sur-Mer">Boulogne-sur-Mer</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/52nd_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="52nd Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">52nd Brigade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/17th_(Northern)_Division" title="17th (Northern) Division">17th (Northern) Division</a> in July 1915 also for service on the Western Front while the 10th (Service) Battalion landed at <a href="/wiki/Le_Havre" title="Le Havre">Le Havre</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/69th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="69th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">69th Brigade</a> in the <a href="/wiki/23rd_(Northumbrian)_Division" title="23rd (Northumbrian) Division">23rd Division</a> in August 1915 also for service on the Western Front.<sup id="cite_ref-trail_54-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trail-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Inter-war_.281919.E2.80.931938.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter-war_(1919–1938)">Inter-war (1919–1938)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Inter-war (1919–1938)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1919, the 1st Battalion took part in the <a href="/wiki/Third_Anglo-Afghan_War" title="Third Anglo-Afghan War">Third Anglo-Afghan War</a> and eventually returned home in 1921.<sup id="cite_ref-ww1_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww1-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Regiment's title altered slightly in 1921 to <b>Duke of Wellington's Regiment (West Riding)</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-preamble_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-preamble-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1930s the increasing need for anti-aircraft (AA) defence for Britain's cities was addressed by converting a number of TA infantry battalions into searchlight battalions of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Engineers" title="Royal Engineers">Royal Engineers</a> (RE). The 5th Duke of Wellington's was one unit selected for this role, becoming <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rifles" title="Huddersfield Rifles">43rd (5th Duke of Wellington's) Anti-Aircraft Battalion, Royal Engineers</a> in 1936, retaining its Duke of Wellington's cap badges.<sup id="cite_ref-Regts5_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts5-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Litchfield_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litchfield-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1938, the 4th Battalion at Halifax was converted into <b>58th (Duke of Wellingtons Regiment) Anti-Tank Regiment, Royal Artillery</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Litchfield_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litchfield-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Regts4_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts4-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> A duplicate unit, the 68th Anti-Tank Regiment, Royal Artillery was formed in 1939, with headquarters at Cleckheaton.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1st_Battalion">1st Battalion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 1st Battalion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> was declared on 3 September 1939, and the 1st Battalion, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_colonel_(United_Kingdom)" title="Lieutenant colonel (United Kingdom)">Lieutenant Colonel</a> <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Charles_Beard" title="Edmund Charles Beard">Edmund Charles Beard</a>, was immediately sent to <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/3rd_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="3rd Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">3rd Infantry Brigade</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1st_Infantry_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="1st Infantry Division (United Kingdom)">1st Infantry Division</a> of <a href="/wiki/I_Corps_(United_Kingdom)" title="I Corps (United Kingdom)">1st Corps</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Expeditionary_Force_(World_War_II)" title="British Expeditionary Force (World War II)">BEF</a>. During the retreat to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dunkirk" title="Battle of Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a>, the 'Dukes' formed part of the rearguard.<sup id="cite_ref-ww2_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww2-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 'Dukes' fought in the <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="North African Campaign">North African Campaign</a>, fighting with distinction in a number of actions and gaining several Battle Honours, as part of the 3rd Infantry Brigade. They fought at the Battle of Medjez Plain and the Battle of Banana Ridge and in the Battle of Djebel bou Aoukaz. The <i>Bou</i> was a ridge dominating the <a href="/wiki/Majaz_al_Bab" title="Majaz al Bab">Medjez el Bab</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a> road.<sup id="cite_ref-ww2_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww2-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 'Dukes' also fought in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italian Campaign</a>. They took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Anzio" title="Battle of Anzio">Anzio Campaign</a>, in an attempt to outflank the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Line" title="Winter Line">Gustav Line</a> and force a German retreat from <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Monte_Cassino" title="Battle of Monte Cassino">Monte Cassino</a>. The 'Dukes' fought with distinction at the Battle of Monte Ceco in October 1944 where Captain <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Burns_(police_officer)" title="Arthur Burns (police officer)">Arthur Burns</a> was awarded a <a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Order" title="Distinguished Service Order">DSO</a> and Private <a href="/wiki/Richard_Henry_Burton" title="Richard Henry Burton">Richard Henry Burton</a> of the 1st Battalion was awarded a <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Cross" title="Victoria Cross">Victoria Cross</a> for his courageous action in the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-ww2_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww2-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 221.33333333333px"><div style="width: 221.33333333333px">
