<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2nd_Battalion">2nd Battalion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2nd Battalion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>, the 2nd Battalion took part in the rearguard action at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sittang_Bridge" title="Battle of Sittang Bridge">Battle of Sittang Bridge</a> in February 1942. They were trained as <a href="/wiki/Chindits" title="Chindits">Chindits</a>, to operate behind Japanese lines, who were at that time attacking <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, they were formed into two columns, the 33rd and 76th,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> to operate behind the Japanese lines during the fierce battles for <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Imphal" title="Battle of Imphal">Imphal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kohima" title="Battle of Kohima">Kohima</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ww2_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ww2-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="58th_.28Duke_of_Wellingtons.29_Anti-Tank_Regiment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="58th_(Duke_of_Wellingtons)_Anti-Tank_Regiment">58th (Duke of Wellingtons) Anti-Tank Regiment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 58th (Duke of Wellingtons) Anti-Tank Regiment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The regiment served in <a href="/wiki/North_African_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="North African Campaign">North Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_Civil_War#From_the_Lebanon_conference_to_the_outbreak" title="Greek Civil War">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria#After_World_War_II" title="Austria">Austria</a> during the war.<sup id="cite_ref-Litchfield_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litchfield-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="43rd_AA_.285th_Duke_of_Wellingtons.29_Battalion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="43rd_AA_(5th_Duke_of_Wellingtons)_Battalion">43rd AA (5th Duke of Wellingtons) Battalion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 43rd AA (5th Duke of Wellingtons) Battalion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><dl><dd><i>See main article <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rifles" title="Huddersfield Rifles">Huddersfield Rifles</a></i></dd></dl></dd></dl>
<p>43rd AA Battalion served in <a href="/wiki/31st_(North_Midland)_Anti-Aircraft_Brigade" title="31st (North Midland) Anti-Aircraft Brigade">31st (North Midland) Anti-Aircraft Brigade</a>, protecting West Yorkshire during the <a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">Blitz</a>. In 1940 the RE AA battalions were transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Artillery" title="Royal Artillery">Royal Artillery</a>, and it became the <b>43rd (5th Duke of Wellington's) Searchlight Regiment, Royal Artillery</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Regts5_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts5-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Litchfield_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litchfield-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1944 the regiment was assigned to <a href="/wiki/21st_Army_Group" title="21st Army Group">21st Army Group</a> preparing for the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Normandy Campaign</a>. In the event, the regiment did not take  part. However, by the autumn of 1944, the German <i><a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a></i> was suffering from such shortages of pilots, aircraft and fuel that serious aerial attacks on the UK could be discounted. At the same time 21st Army Group was experiencing a severe manpower shortage, particularly among the infantry. The <a href="/wiki/War_Office" title="War Office">War Office</a> began to reorganise surplus AA regiments in the UK into infantry units, primarily for duties in the rear areas, thereby releasing trained infantry for frontline service.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On 1 October 1944, 43rd S/L Rgt was converted into <b>43rd (5th Bn Duke of Wellingtons) Garrison Regiment, RA</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Regts5_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts5-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Litchfield_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litchfield-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Garrison_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garrison-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FarnM_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FarnM-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> A month later, it was reorganised as an infantry battalion and redesignated <b>600th Regiment RA (5th Bn Duke of Wellingtons)</b>. It was the first such RA infantry regiment formed, and was sent to join <a href="/wiki/Second_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="Second Army (United Kingdom)">Second Army</a> in NW Europe for line of communication duties.<sup id="cite_ref-Regts5_58-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts5-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Litchfield_59-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litchfield-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Garrison_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garrison-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-600RA_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-600RA-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The unit was placed in 'suspended animation' in February 1945 and its personnel drafted to other units.<sup id="cite_ref-Litchfield_59-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litchfield-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-600RA_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-600RA-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1.2F6th_and_1.2F7th_battalions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1/6th_and_1/7th_battalions">1/6th and 1/7th battalions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 1/6th and 1/7th battalions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1/6th and 1/7th battalions of the regiment were both assigned to the <a href="/wiki/147th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="147th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">147th Infantry Brigade</a>, alongside the 1/5th <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Regiment" title="West Yorkshire Regiment">West Yorkshire Regiment</a>, which itself was part of the <a href="/wiki/49th_(West_Riding)_Infantry_Division" title="49th (West Riding) Infantry Division">49th (West Riding) Infantry Division</a>. The brigade did not see service with the rest of the division in the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Campaign">Norwegian Campaign</a>, but were instead sent to <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> after it was <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Iceland" title="Invasion of Iceland">invaded in 1940</a>, and remained there until May 1942 when it was transferred back to the United Kingdom. On 28 February 1943, both battalions lost the '1/' prefix, becoming, simply, the 6th and 7th battalions, respectively. They both <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Normandy" title="Invasion of Normandy">landed in Normandy</a> on 12 June 1944 shortly after the <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">D-Day landings of 6 June</a>. They fought in the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Battle of Normandy</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Army_(United_Kingdom)" title="Second Army (United Kingdom)">British Second Army</a> in its attempts to <a href="/wiki/Battle_for_Caen" title="Battle for Caen">capture the city of Caen</a>. In particular, the 6th Battalion was severely mauled during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Martlet" title="Operation Martlet">Operation Martlet</a> and, due to the heavy casualties sustained, was returned to the United Kingdom and disbanded, most of its men being sent to the 7th Battalion. They were replaced in the brigade by the 1st Battalion, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Leicestershire_Regiment" title="Royal Leicestershire Regiment">Leicestershire Regiment</a>. The 7th DWR continued to fight in the Normandy Campaign in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_the_Odon" title="Second Battle of the Odon">Second Battle of the Odon</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Clearing_the_Channel_Ports&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Clearing the Channel Ports (page does not exist)">clearing the Channel Ports</a> in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Astonia" title="Operation Astonia">Operation Astonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the failure of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Market_Garden" title="Operation Market Garden">Operation Market Garden</a>, the 7th Battalion was stationed at the <a href="/wiki/Nijmegen" title="Nijmegen">Nijmegen</a> bridgehead, in late November, and around <a href="/wiki/Haalderen" title="Haalderen">Haalderen</a>. Just after midnight of 1 December the Battalion was being hit by heavy artillery, mortar and <a href="/wiki/MG_42" title="MG 42">Spandau</a> fire. As the night progressed they came under attack from multiple infantry elements of the <a href="/wiki/6th_Parachute_Division_(Germany)" title="6th Parachute Division (Germany)">German 6th Parachute Division</a> in an attempt to capture the <a href="/wiki/Nijmegen" title="Nijmegen">Nijmegen</a> bridge. Fighting intensified, taking in house to house fighting throughout Haalderen and <a href="/wiki/Gendt" title="Gendt">Gendt</a> During the nights of 3–4 December, with small arms and grenades, with the Dukes 'A Company' Headquarters in the village school. Fighting was very confused and movement limited due to heavy flooding of the ground from the breached canals and river.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> A German officer, 2nd Lieutenant Heinich, 5 Coy 16 Parachute Regiment, was captured by members of 'B' company, who were laying trip flares. Major <a href="/wiki/Denis_Hamilton" title="Denis Hamilton">Denis Hamilton</a> (who was in temporary command of the battalion) quickly organised a defence, using his Bren Gun Carriers, to hold back the Germans. Over 100 prisoners, with a further 50 killed or wounded were taken from the 5th, 7th and 10th companies of the German 16 Para Regiment. By 6 December the attack had died out and the Dukes were relieved by the 11th Battalion, Royal Scots Fusiliers. 7DWR moved into reserve in <a href="/wiki/Bemmel" title="Bemmel">Bemmel</a> where they received sporadic shelling from heavy artillery, whilst putting out patrols to guard against a potential water borne attack on the Nijmegen bridge.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The next notable service seen by the battalion was in the <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_Arnhem" title="Liberation of Arnhem">Liberation of Arnhem</a> in April 1945, shortly before <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">Victory in Europe Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2.2F6th_and_2.2F7th_battalions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2/6th_and_2/7th_battalions">2/6th and 2/7th battalions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 2/6th and 2/7th battalions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Throughout the spring and summer of 1939, the <a href="/wiki/Army_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="Army Reserve (United Kingdom)">Territorial Army</a> was ordered to expand in size and double its strength by creating duplicate units and, as a result, the 6th and 7th battalions created duplicate units, the 2/6th and 2/7th battalions. Both battalions became part of the <a href="/wiki/137th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="137th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">137th Infantry Brigade</a>, attached to the <a href="/wiki/46th_Infantry_Division_(United_Kingdom)" title="46th Infantry Division (United Kingdom)">46th (West Riding and North Midland) Infantry Division</a> and were sent overseas to France in April 1940 to join the <a href="/wiki/British_Expeditionary_Force_(World_War_II)" title="British Expeditionary Force (World War II)">British Expeditionary Force</a>. Poorly trained and equipped, both battalions were battered during the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(Wehrmacht)" class="mw-redirect" title="German Army (Wehrmacht)">German Army</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Blitzkrieg" title="Blitzkrieg">blitzkrieg</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">Battle of France</a> and were forced to <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dunkirk" title="Battle of Dunkirk">retreat to Dunkirk</a> and be <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_evacuation" title="Dunkirk evacuation">evacuated to England</a>. The battalions spent the next two years on home defence, preparing for a <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sea_Lion" title="Operation Sea Lion">German invasion</a> which never arrived. In July 1942 these battalions were transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Armoured_Corps" title="Royal Armoured Corps">Royal Armoured Corps</a> and converted to armour as <a href="/w/index.php?title=114th_Regiment_Royal_Armoured_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="114th Regiment Royal Armoured Corps (page does not exist)">114 RAC</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=115th_Regiment_Royal_Armoured_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="115th Regiment Royal Armoured Corps (page does not exist)">115 RAC</a>. They continued to wear their Duke's badge on the black beret of the Royal Armoured Corps.<sup id="cite_ref-Forty_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forty-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="8th_Battalion">8th Battalion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 8th Battalion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The regiment's 8th Battalion was raised in July 1940 and in 1941 it was also converted to a tank unit becoming <a href="/wiki/145th_Regiment_Royal_Armoured_Corps" title="145th Regiment Royal Armoured Corps">145th Regiment RAC (8th DWR)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Forty_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forty-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The regiment served in <a href="/wiki/21st_Army_Tank_Brigade" title="21st Army Tank Brigade">21st Army Tank Brigade</a>, equipped with <a href="/wiki/Churchill_tank" title="Churchill tank">Churchill tanks</a>. It joined 1st Army in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> and was transferred to <a href="/wiki/25th_Army_Tank_Brigade" title="25th Army Tank Brigade">25th Army Tank Brigade</a> in support of <a href="/wiki/24th_Infantry_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="24th Infantry Brigade (United Kingdom)">24 Guards Brigade (1st Division)</a> on the push through <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> It was one of the units in support of the Dukes 1st Battalion and the <a href="/wiki/Loyal_Regiment_(North_Lancashire)" title="Loyal Regiment (North Lancashire)">Loyal Regiment (North Lancashire)</a> at the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Banana_Ridge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of Banana Ridge (page does not exist)">Battle of Banana Ridge</a>, over looking the <a href="/wiki/Majaz_al_Bab" title="Majaz al Bab">Medjez el Bab plain</a>, as the front part of a five-mile-wide divisional offensive to advance on <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>. The battle on the ridge resulted in the 1st Dukes and the QLR's being the only units to be award the battle honour <b>Banana Ridge</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> A following battle resulted in the award of the battle honour <b>Djebel Bou Aoukaz</b> on the 1st Dukes, the 1st <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Shropshire_Light_Infantry" title="King&#39;s Shropshire Light Infantry">King's Shropshire Light Infantry</a> and <b>145th Regiment RAC (8th DWR)</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="9th_Battalion">9th Battalion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 9th Battalion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 9th Battalion was also converted to armour, becoming <a href="/w/index.php?title=146th_Regiment_RAC_(DWR)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="146th Regiment RAC (DWR) (page does not exist)">146th Regiment RAC (DWR)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Forty_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forty-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar">Postwar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Postwar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When the TA was reformed in 1947, the 4th, 5th and 6th Battalions became the <b>382nd (Duke of Wellington's Regiment) Anti-Tank Regiment</b> (later Medium Regiment), <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rifles" title="Huddersfield Rifles">578th (5th Bn, The Duke of Wellington's Regiment) Heavy Anti-Aircraft Regiment</a>, and <b>673rd (Duke of Wellington's Regiment) Light Anti-Aircraft Regiment</b> respectively of the Royal Artillery. In 1955 the three regiments merged into the 382nd, each providing one battery. In 1957 some of the 5th Bn battery transferred to the 7th Bn (still in the infantry role) and formed the 5/7th Bn, thereby bringing together both parts of the former 2nd Volunteer Bn. Finally, in 1961, the rest of 382 Rgt converted to infantry and merged with the 5/7th Bn, bringing together all four Territorial battalions of the regiment as the <b>West Riding Battalion</b>, which in 1967 became part of the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Volunteers" title="Yorkshire Volunteers">Yorkshire Volunteers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Regts7_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts7-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Regts5_58-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts5-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Litchfield_59-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litchfield-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Regts4_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Regts4-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Korean_War_.281952.E2.80.931956.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Korean_War_(1952–1956)">Korean War (1952–1956)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Korean War (1952–1956)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 1st Battalion was deployed to <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> in 1952, two years after the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> had broken out. They were part of the <a href="/wiki/1st_Commonwealth_Division" title="1st Commonwealth Division">1st Commonwealth Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_The_Hook">Battle of The Hook</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Battle of The Hook">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Third_Battle_of_the_Hook" title="Third Battle of the Hook">Third Battle of the Hook</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_the_Hook_28-29_May_1953.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Battle_of_the_Hook_28-29_May_1953.png/220px-Battle_of_the_Hook_28-29_May_1953.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Battle_of_the_Hook_28-29_May_1953.png/330px-Battle_of_the_Hook_28-29_May_1953.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Battle_of_the_Hook_28-29_May_1953.png/440px-Battle_of_the_Hook_28-29_May_1953.png 2x" data-file-width="2039" data-file-height="1404" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_the_Hook_28-29_May_1953.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Successive Chinese assaults on the Hook position on the night of 28–29 May 1953. Redrawn from poor quality sketch maps filed with 1DWR Regimental War Diaries, archived as WO/308/53 at the Public Record Office, London</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Men_of_the_1st_Battalion,_The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment,_have_a_smoke_while_waiting_for_dusk_to_fall_before_joining_a_patrol_into_no-man%27s_land_at_The_Hook.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Men_of_the_1st_Battalion%2C_The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment%2C_have_a_smoke_while_waiting_for_dusk_to_fall_before_joining_a_patrol_into_no-man%27s_land_at_The_Hook.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Men_of_the_1st_Battalion%2C_The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment%2C_have_a_smoke_while_waiting_for_dusk_to_fall_before_joining_a_patrol_into_no-man%27s_land_at_The_Hook.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Men_of_the_1st_Battalion%2C_The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment%2C_have_a_smoke_while_waiting_for_dusk_to_fall_before_joining_a_patrol_into_no-man%27s_land_at_The_Hook.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="596" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Men_of_the_1st_Battalion,_The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment,_have_a_smoke_while_waiting_for_dusk_to_fall_before_joining_a_patrol_into_no-man%27s_land_at_The_Hook.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Men of the 1st Battalion, The Duke of Wellington's Regiment in Korea</div></div></div>
<p>In 1953, the 1st Battalion relieved the <a href="/wiki/Black_Watch" title="Black Watch">Black Watch</a>, who had been <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_the_Hook" title="Second Battle of the Hook">defending a position</a> known as The Hook, a crescent shaped ridge, which was of tactical importance in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> sector. The third Battle of the Hook began on 28 May. An initial bombardment of the British positions took place, with the Chinese forces charging the forward British positions once the bombardment ceased. The fighting that ensued was bloody and more akin to the battles that the 'Dukes' had fought in the First World War. Shells were now raining down on the Hook from artillery and mortars, from both the Chinese and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> forces. The Chinese launched a second attack but were cut down by heavy fire from UN the forces. Further attacks occurred on 28 May, but all were defeated in heavy fighting. Just 30 minutes into 29 May, the Chinese forces launched another attack but, as before, they were beaten back. Alma Company of 'The 'Dukes' then began advancing up the line of the original trenches to dislodge the remaining Chinese forces in the forward trenches. The 'Dukes' secured the Hook at 3:30&#160;a.m. The 'Dukes' losses were three officers and 17 other ranks killed and two officers and 84 other ranks wounded, plus 20 other ranks missing.<sup id="cite_ref-Korean_War_Battle_of_The_Hook_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Korean_War_Battle_of_The_Hook-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 'Dukes' embarked for <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> on 13 November 1953, arriving on 10 December. In May 1954, during a visit to Gibraltar by Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Elizabeth II</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Duke of Edinburgh">Duke of Edinburgh</a>, the Commanding Officer of the 'Dukes' (Lieutenant Colonel FR St P Bunbury) and a further 10 officers and other ranks received decorations for their actions in Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Post-Korean_War_.281956.E2.80.932005.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Korean_War_(1956–2005)">Post-Korean War (1956–2005)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Post-Korean War (1956–2005)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Garrison_duties">Garrison duties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Garrison duties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the bloody encounters in the Korean War, the 'Dukes' were occupied by a series of garrison duties. The 'Dukes' were first deployed to <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, then to <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> in 1956, where they participated in anti-terrorist operations against <a href="/wiki/EOKA" title="EOKA">EOKA</a>. The following year, the 'Dukes' deployed to <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. They moved back to the mainland in 1959, joining the new UK Strategic Reserve, as part of <a href="/wiki/19th_Light_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="19th Light Brigade (United Kingdom)">19 Infantry Brigade)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cold_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cold-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> On 6 August 1959 the Regimental Depot, at Wellesley Barracks, was closed down. training of new recruits was undertaken at the Kings Division depot at <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_Barracks,_Strensall" title="Queen Elizabeth Barracks, Strensall">Strensall Barracks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 'Dukes' returned to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">UK</a> in 1970. Then deployed to Northern Ireland a number of times during The Troubles. In one deployment in 1972 three soldiers were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-cold_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cold-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1985, the 'Dukes' deployed to <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> for a six-month tour of duty, taking part in operation 'Holdfast'.<sup id="cite_ref-cold_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cold-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In 1987 the 'Dukes' deployed again to Northern Ireland for a two-year tour, based in Palace Barracks, just outside the City of Belfast.<sup id="cite_ref-cold_91-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cold-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Bosnia_.281994.E2.80.931995.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_(1994–1995)">Bosnia (1994–1995)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Bosnia (1994–1995)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 1994, the 'Dukes' deployed to <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia</a>, with an area of responsibility covering <a href="/wiki/Bugojno" title="Bugojno">Bugojno</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitez" title="Vitez">Vitez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Travnik" title="Travnik">Travnik</a> and the besieged <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">enclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gora%C5%BEde" title="Goražde">Goražde</a>. The latter was under siege for much of the war. It was declared a <a href="/w/index.php?title=UN_Safe_Zone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="UN Safe Zone (page does not exist)">UN Safe Zone</a> in that year. The 'Dukes' were one of the first units to enter the town. The Regiment pushed the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bosnian-Serb_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bosnian-Serb Army (page does not exist)">Bosnian-Serb Army</a> from their positions around the town to a distance of over one mile. Their objective in doing this was to create a safe zone for the town. While at Goražde, Private Shaun Taylor of C Company was killed during an engagement with Bosnian-Serb forces while manning an observation post. The engagement lasted fifteen minutes, with over 2,000 rounds of ammunition being expended by the 'Dukes'. Seven of the Bosnian-Serb soldiers were killed in the fire-fight. Goražde remained a safe zone, being held by British troops from 1994 to 1995. It was the only safe zone to survive the war and avoided the tragedies that occurred in other UN safe zones such as <a href="/wiki/Srebrenica" title="Srebrenica">Srebrenica</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDepa" title="Žepa">Žepa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-world_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:P8191754_CSgt_Wayne_Mills.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/P8191754_CSgt_Wayne_Mills.JPG/220px-P8191754_CSgt_Wayne_Mills.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="348" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/P8191754_CSgt_Wayne_Mills.JPG/330px-P8191754_CSgt_Wayne_Mills.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/P8191754_CSgt_Wayne_Mills.JPG/440px-P8191754_CSgt_Wayne_Mills.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1086" data-file-height="1716" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:P8191754_CSgt_Wayne_Mills.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>'C/Sgt Wayne Mills</div></div></div>
<p>Corporal <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Mills_(British_Army_soldier)" title="Wayne Mills (British Army soldier)">Wayne Mills</a> of the 1st Battalion became the first recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Conspicuous_Gallantry_Cross" title="Conspicuous Gallantry Cross">Conspicuous Gallantry Cross</a>, second only to the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Cross" title="Victoria Cross">Victoria Cross</a>. On (29 April 1994), a patrol led by Corporal Mills came under heavy small-arms fire from a group of Bosnian-Serbs. The patrol returned fire, killing two of the attackers. The patrol then withdrew, but the attackers persisted in firing on the patrol. The patrol soon reached an open clearing, where it was obvious they would be highly vulnerable to fire from the attackers. Corporal Mills then performed an astonishing feat of bravery. He turned back and engaged the group in a fire-fight, delaying the attackers long enough to allow the rest of his patrol to cross the clearing. While doing this brave act, Corporal Mills shot the leader of the group, with the rest scattering into the woods. Due to that action he returned to his patrol safely, who were giving covering fire.<sup id="cite_ref-world_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lieutenant-Colonel <a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Santa-Olalla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="David Santa-Olalla (page does not exist)">David Santa-Olalla</a> received the <a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Service_Order" title="Distinguished Service Order">Distinguished Service Order</a> for his inspirational leadership and courage during the 'Dukes' deployment to Bosnia. He arranged for the mutual withdrawal of both Serbian and Muslim forces, from the besieged town of Goražde, just as the <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> talks were being held on the town.<sup id="cite_ref-world_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1995.E2.80.932005"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1995–2005">1995–2005</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 1995–2005">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 1995, the 'Dukes' were again posted to Northern Ireland for a two-year tour of duty.<sup id="cite_ref-world_93-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In March 1997, a composite company from the 1st Battalion was deployed to the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>. In 1998, C Company deployed for a tour of duty in <a href="/wiki/County_Armagh" title="County Armagh">South Armagh</a>. During the period 1998–2000, the 1st Battalion served as a <a href="/wiki/Public_duties" title="Public duties">public duties</a> unit in London.<sup id="cite_ref-world_93-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2001, a company from the 'Dukes' deployed to <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, with the objective of preventing arms and munitions being transported from <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> into Kosovo, then onto the Former Yugolav Republic Of Macedonia, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-world_93-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003, the 'Dukes' were part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Telic" title="Operation Telic">Operation Telic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq</a>, as part of <a href="/wiki/1_(United_Kingdom)_Armoured_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="1 (United Kingdom) Armoured Division">1 (United Kingdom) Armoured Division</a>. The 'Dukes' returned, as part of  <a href="/wiki/4th_Mechanized_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="4th Mechanized Brigade (United Kingdom)">4 (Armoured) Brigade</a>, to the South-East of Iraq, in October 2004, to join the British-led <a href="/wiki/Multi-National_Division_(South-East)_(Iraq)" title="Multi-National Division (South-East) (Iraq)">Multi-National Division (South-East)</a>, as a fully equipped armoured infantry battalion with Warrior Armoured Personnel Carriers.<sup id="cite_ref-world_93-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Timothy_Taylors_Havercake_Ale_Beer_Bottle_(RLH).gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Timothy_Taylors_Havercake_Ale_Beer_Bottle_%28RLH%29.gif/220px-Timothy_Taylors_Havercake_Ale_Beer_Bottle_%28RLH%29.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="547" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Timothy_Taylors_Havercake_Ale_Beer_Bottle_%28RLH%29.gif/330px-Timothy_Taylors_Havercake_Ale_Beer_Bottle_%28RLH%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Timothy_Taylors_Havercake_Ale_Beer_Bottle_%28RLH%29.gif/440px-Timothy_Taylors_Havercake_Ale_Beer_Bottle_%28RLH%29.gif 2x" data-file-width="936" data-file-height="2328" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Timothy_Taylors_Havercake_Ale_Beer_Bottle_(RLH).gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Havercake Ale</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DWR_Colours,_Erquinghem_Lys,_France_(RLH)_2005-11-12.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/DWR_Colours%2C_Erquinghem_Lys%2C_France_%28RLH%29_2005-11-12.JPG/220px-DWR_Colours%2C_Erquinghem_Lys%2C_France_%28RLH%29_2005-11-12.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/DWR_Colours%2C_Erquinghem_Lys%2C_France_%28RLH%29_2005-11-12.JPG/330px-DWR_Colours%2C_Erquinghem_Lys%2C_France_%28RLH%29_2005-11-12.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/DWR_Colours%2C_Erquinghem_Lys%2C_France_%28RLH%29_2005-11-12.JPG/440px-DWR_Colours%2C_Erquinghem_Lys%2C_France_%28RLH%29_2005-11-12.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="989" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DWR_Colours,_Erquinghem_Lys,_France_(RLH)_2005-11-12.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>DWR Drums platoon lead the Regiment to Erquinghem Lys Town Hall to receive the Keys to The town.</div></div></div>
<p>During 2003, in <a href="/wiki/Osnabr%C3%BCck" title="Osnabrück">Osnabrück</a>, Germany, where the 'Dukes' were then based, the Regiment celebrated its 300th year in existence. Over 2000 past and present members converged on the town to take part in the celebrations. The 'Dukes' were presented with new <a href="/wiki/Colours,_standards_and_guidons" class="mw-redirect" title="Colours, standards and guidons">colours</a> by HM Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Elizabeth II</a>, represented by The Colonel of The Regiment <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_John_Webb-Carter" class="mw-redirect" title="Evelyn John Webb-Carter">Major-General Sir Evelyn John Webb-Carter KCB</a>, due to the ill health of the Queen's representative, the regiments <a href="/wiki/Colonel-in-Chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonel-in-Chief">Colonel-in-Chief</a> the Duke of Wellington.<sup id="cite_ref-world_93-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The regiment had a <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a> called Havercake Ale named in their honour by the <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Taylor_Brewery" title="Timothy Taylor Brewery">Timothy Taylor Brewery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keighley" title="Keighley">Keighley</a>, to mark the regiment's tercentenary. Timothy Taylor, the founder of the brewery, had served in an antecedent unit of the regiment during 1859. Since then other members of the family and employees had also enlisted as a 'Duke'.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 12 November 2005, the Regiment was awarded the "Keys to the Town" of <a href="/wiki/Erquinghem-Lys" title="Erquinghem-Lys">Erquinghem-Lys</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Amalgamation">Amalgamation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Amalgamation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2004, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Delivering_Security_in_a_Changing_World" title="Delivering Security in a Changing World">re-organisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a>, it was announced that the Duke of Wellington's Regiment would be amalgamated with the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales%27s_Own_Regiment_of_Yorkshire" title="Prince of Wales&#39;s Own Regiment of Yorkshire">Prince of Wales's Own Regiment of Yorkshire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/The_Green_Howards" class="mw-redirect" title="The Green Howards">Green Howards</a>', all <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>-based regiments in the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Division" title="King&#39;s Division">King's Division</a>, to form the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Regiment" title="Yorkshire Regiment">Yorkshire Regiment</a>. The re-badging parade took place on 6 June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 'Dukes' had five companies, named to commemorate five significant campaigns and battles, in which the Dukes took part and were awarded a <a href="/wiki/Battle_honour" title="Battle honour">Battle honour</a>, which have been retained by the battalion in the Yorkshire Regiment:<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>A Company&#160;— Alma&#160;— commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alma" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Alma">Battle of Alma</a>, during the Crimean War 1853–1856</dd>
<dd>B Company&#160;— Burma&#160;— commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Burma_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma Campaign">Burma Campaign</a>, during the Second World War 1941–1944</dd>
<dd>C Company&#160;— Corunna&#160;— commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Corunna" title="Battle of Corunna">Battle of Corunna</a>, during the Peninsular War of 1809–1813</dd>
<dd>Support Company&#160;— Somme&#160;— commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Battle of the Somme</a>, during the First World War 1914–1918</dd>
<dd>Headquarter Company&#160;— Hook&#160;— commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Hook" title="Battle of the Hook">Battle of the Hook</a>, during the Korean war 1952–1953</dd></dl>
<p>When required an additional rifle company was formed:- D Company — Dettingen — commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dettingen" title="Battle of Dettingen">Battle of Dettingen</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> in 1743 and an additional administration company:- W Company — Waterloo — commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterloo Campaign">Waterloo campaign</a> in 1815. Both companies having previously existed during the Dukes existence.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regimental_colours">Regimental colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Regimental colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:P6060065_(RLH-DWR-3YR).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/P6060065_%28RLH-DWR-3YR%29.JPG/200px-P6060065_%28RLH-DWR-3YR%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/P6060065_%28RLH-DWR-3YR%29.JPG/300px-P6060065_%28RLH-DWR-3YR%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/P6060065_%28RLH-DWR-3YR%29.JPG/400px-P6060065_%28RLH-DWR-3YR%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1197" data-file-height="649" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:P6060065_(RLH-DWR-3YR).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><b>Dukes</b> final morning parade before rebadging (6 June 2006)</div></div></div>
<p>The Duke of Wellington's Regiment had four <a href="/wiki/Colours,_standards_and_guidons" class="mw-redirect" title="Colours, standards and guidons">colours</a> on parade. The first pair of colours were the standard set of Regulation Colours, which all Regiments are presented with. The second pair was a set of Honorary Colours, which were originally presented to the 76th Regiment of Foot in 1808 for their actions during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ally_Ghur" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Ally Ghur">Battle of Ally Ghur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> in 1803.<sup id="cite_ref-colours_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colours-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DWR_Regimental_Colours_RLH.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/DWR_Regimental_Colours_RLH.jpg/200px-DWR_Regimental_Colours_RLH.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="63" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/DWR_Regimental_Colours_RLH.jpg/300px-DWR_Regimental_Colours_RLH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/DWR_Regimental_Colours_RLH.jpg/400px-DWR_Regimental_Colours_RLH.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="719" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DWR_Regimental_Colours_RLH.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>click on image to enlarge</div></div></div>
<p>The Honorary Colours were approximately 6-foot 6 inch by 6-foot. Following rebadging, on 6 June 2006, the 3rd Battalion the Yorkshire Regiment (Duke of Wellington's) inherited responsibility for parading the Honorary Colours. On 31 March 2007 the Regulation colours were taken out of service and laid up in <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a> Parish church. There was a short ceremony in the church grounds where the troops were inspected by the <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">Mayor</a> of Halifax, Councillor Colin Stout, and the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lieutenant_of_West_Yorkshire" title="Lord Lieutenant of West Yorkshire">Lord Lieutenant of West Yorkshire</a> Dr Ingrid Roscoe.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2007-03-31_Colours_1DWR_Halifax(RLH).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/2007-03-31_Colours_1DWR_Halifax%28RLH%29.JPG/200px-2007-03-31_Colours_1DWR_Halifax%28RLH%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/2007-03-31_Colours_1DWR_Halifax%28RLH%29.JPG/300px-2007-03-31_Colours_1DWR_Halifax%28RLH%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/2007-03-31_Colours_1DWR_Halifax%28RLH%29.JPG/400px-2007-03-31_Colours_1DWR_Halifax%28RLH%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2580" data-file-height="2580" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2007-03-31_Colours_1DWR_Halifax(RLH).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Regimental Colours of the 1st Battalion, Duke of Wellington's Regiment (West Riding), in Halifax Parish Church</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regimental_museum">Regimental museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Regimental museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Duke of Wellington's Regiment Museum is based at <a href="/wiki/Bankfield_Museum" title="Bankfield Museum">Bankfield House</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a>, Yorkshire.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_honours">Battle honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Battle honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The regiment’s battle honours were as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-regimentsDoW_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regimentsDoW-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniforms">Uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On formation in 1702 as the Earl of Huntingdon's Regiment a red coat lined with yellow was worn, together with yellow breeches. Later in the 18th Century the coats had red <a href="/wiki/Facings" class="mw-redirect" title="Facings">facings</a> but white linings which showed in the turn-backed skirts. For the remainder of its history the Regiment was unusual in that the collars, cuffs and shoulder straps of its red coats were also red (most British regiments had facings of contrasting colours). This continued to be the case with the scarlet tunic worn by all ranks in full dress until 1914 and by bandsmen until amalgamation (see illustrations above). Officers were distinguished by silver buttons and braid until 1830 and thereafter by gold, After 1893 the badge of the Duke of Wellington was worn.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alliances">Alliances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Alliances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Affiliation_Plaque,_LVQ-DWR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Affiliation_Plaque%2C_LVQ-DWR.jpg/220px-Affiliation_Plaque%2C_LVQ-DWR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Affiliation_Plaque%2C_LVQ-DWR.jpg/330px-Affiliation_Plaque%2C_LVQ-DWR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Affiliation_Plaque%2C_LVQ-DWR.jpg/440px-Affiliation_Plaque%2C_LVQ-DWR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2184" data-file-height="2719" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Affiliation_Plaque,_LVQ-DWR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>DWR &amp; les Voltigeurs de Québec Regimental affiliation plague</div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Les_Voltigeurs_de_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Les Voltigeurs de Québec">les Voltigeurs de Québec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a></li>
<li>10th Battalion, The <a href="/wiki/Baloch_Regiment" title="Baloch Regiment">Baloch Regiment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HMS_Iron_Duke_(F234)" title="HMS Iron Duke (F234)">HMS <i>Iron Duke</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Victoria_Cross_recipients">Victoria Cross recipients</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Victoria Cross recipients">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Victoria Cross recipients have been:<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Drummer" title="Drummer">Drummer</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Magner" title="Michael Magner">Michael Magner</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Private_(rank)" title="Private (rank)">Private</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Bergin" title="James Bergin">James Bergin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sergeant" title="Sergeant">Sergeant</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Firth" title="James Firth">James Firth</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Second_Lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Lieutenant">Second Lieutenant</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Palmer_Huffam" class="mw-redirect" title="James Palmer Huffam">James Palmer Huffam</a></li>
<li>Second Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kelly_(VC)" title="Henry Kelly (VC)">Henry Kelly</a></li>
<li>Private <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Loosemore" title="Arnold Loosemore">Arnold Loosemore</a></li>
<li>Private <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Poulter" title="Arthur Poulter">Arthur Poulter</a></li>
<li>Private <a href="/wiki/Richard_Henry_Burton" title="Richard Henry Burton">Richard Henry Burton</a></li>
<li>Private <a href="/wiki/Henry_Tandey" title="Henry Tandey">Henry Tandey</a> was awarded his VC for actions during his service with the 'Dukes' and donated his medals to the Regimental Museum in Halifax, West Yorkshire. On special occasions and parades he would sign them out to wear. The last time he signed them out he died. Unknowingly, the medals were sold and a private collector subsequently presented the medals to the Regimental Museum of <a href="/wiki/The_Green_Howards" class="mw-redirect" title="The Green Howards">The Green Howards</a>, a regiment in which he had earlier served.</li>
<li>Acting-Sergeant <a href="/wiki/Hanson_Victor_Turner" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanson Victor Turner">Hanson Victor Turner</a> – originally a member of the regiment, he was serving with <a href="/wiki/The_West_Yorkshire_Regiment_(The_Prince_of_Wales%27s_Own)" class="mw-redirect" title="The West Yorkshire Regiment (The Prince of Wales&#39;s Own)">The West Yorkshire Regiment (The Prince of Wales's Own)</a> when he was awarded his VC. When his medal was put up for sale it was purchased by the Halifax Town Council, as he was a Halifax resident. It is displayed in the Regimental Museum, in Halifax.</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 'Dukes' had a long and proud <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">Rugby</a> tradition. They produced in their history 11 international players, 7 English, 1 Irish and 3 Scottish, with over 50 players capped for the army against the Navy &amp; Air Force since 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-rugby_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rugby-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> they list:- Capt (Bull) Faithfull, England (3 Caps) 1924. Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Horsey_Browne" title="Horsey Browne">WF (Horsey) Brown</a>, Army &amp; Ireland (12 Caps), 1925–1928. Captain <a href="/wiki/Mike_Campbell-Lamerton" title="Mike Campbell-Lamerton">Mike Campbell-Lamerton</a>, Army, London Scottish, Scotland (23 Caps), <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lions" title="British and Irish Lions">British Lions</a> in South Africa in 1962, Captain of the British Lions in Australia &amp; New Zealand in 1966. Lieutenant CF Grieve and FJ Reynolds Toured South Africa in 1938 with the British Lions. In the early 1950s DW Shuttleworth and EMP Hardy provided the Half Back pairing for England. Corporals Waqabaca and Ponjiasi played for <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>. Brigadier DW Shuttleworth became the President of the English Rugby Football Union during the 1985/86 season. In 1957–1959, whilst stationed in Northern Ireland, the 'Dukes' played rugby throughout Ulster. At the end of the tour the Ulster Team honoured the regiment by playing them at <a href="/wiki/Ravenhill_Stadium" title="Ravenhill Stadium">Ravenhill</a>, with the 'Dukes' winning 19 – 8. In 1960 during an emergency posting to Kenya the Kenyan Champions <a href="/wiki/Nakuru" title="Nakuru">Nakuru</a> heard the Dukes were there and challenged them to a match. The <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Regiment" title="Kenya Regiment">Kenya Regiment</a> loaned them their team strip to wear. The 'Dukes' won the match.<sup id="cite_ref-rugby_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rugby-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The regiment's <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> internationals include: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_Curry&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brian Curry (page does not exist)">Brian Curry</a>, England, 1956; <a href="/wiki/Norman_Field" title="Norman Field">Norman Field</a>, GB, 1963; <a href="/wiki/Roy_Sabine" title="Roy Sabine">Roy Sabine</a>, GB; <a href="/wiki/Jack_Scroby" title="Jack Scroby">Jack Scroby</a>, Army 1959, GB <a href="/wiki/Halifax_RLFC" class="mw-redirect" title="Halifax RLFC">Halifax</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Northern</a>; <a href="/wiki/Charles_Renilson" title="Charles Renilson">Charlie Renilson</a>, Scotland, GB, 1965 and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Keegan" title="Arthur Keegan">Arthur 'Ollie' Keegan</a>, GB.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several members of the regiment played cricket for the <a href="/wiki/Free_Foresters_Cricket_Club" title="Free Foresters Cricket Club">Free Foresters Cricket Club</a> and Pte Brian Stead played for the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire County Cricket Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
